</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mass_production" title="Mass production">Mass production</a> of the 2011 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Auris_Hybrid" title="Toyota Auris Hybrid">Toyota Auris Hybrid</a> began in May 2010 at Toyota Manufacturing UK (TMUK) <a href="/wiki/Burnaston" title="Burnaston">Burnaston</a> plant and became the first mass-produced hybrid vehicle to be built in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JustA_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-JustA-82">[82]</a></sup> Sales in the UK began in July 2010, at a price starting at<span style="white-space: nowrap">GB£18,950</span> (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$27,450</span>), <span style="white-space: nowrap">GB£550</span> (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$800</span>) less than the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">Toyota Prius</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edmunds1_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Edmunds1-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The 2011 Auris Hybrid shares the same <a href="/wiki/Powertrain" title="Powertrain">powertrain</a> as the Prius, and combined fuel economy is 74.3 mpg<sub>‑imp</sub> (3.80 L/100 km; 61.9 mpg<sub>‑US</sub>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AurisH_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-AurisH-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2011 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lincoln_MKZ_Hybrid" title="Lincoln MKZ Hybrid">Lincoln MKZ Hybrid</a> was unveiled at the 2010 <a href="/wiki/New_York_International_Auto_Show" title="New York International Auto Show">New York International Auto Show</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC0310_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-GCC0310-89">[89]</a></sup> and sales began in the U.S. in September 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The MKZ Hybrid is the first hybrid version ever to have the same price as the gasoline-engine version of the same car.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Porsche_Cayenne#Hybrid" title="Porsche Cayenne">Porshe Cayenne Hybrid</a> was launched in the U.S in late 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2010_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2010-29">[29]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>2011–2015</dt></dl>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VW_Jetta_Hybrid_WAS_2012_0720.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/VW_Jetta_Hybrid_WAS_2012_0720.JPG/220px-VW_Jetta_Hybrid_WAS_2012_0720.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/VW_Jetta_Hybrid_WAS_2012_0720.JPG/330px-VW_Jetta_Hybrid_WAS_2012_0720.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/VW_Jetta_Hybrid_WAS_2012_0720.JPG/440px-VW_Jetta_Hybrid_WAS_2012_0720.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VW_Jetta_Hybrid_WAS_2012_0720.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2013 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Jetta_Hybrid" title="Volkswagen Jetta Hybrid">Volkswagen Jetta Hybrid</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a> announced at the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Motor_Show#010" title="Geneva Motor Show">2010 Geneva Motor Show</a> the launch of the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Touareg#Touareg_V6_TSI_Hybrid_(2009)" title="Volkswagen Touareg">Touareg Hybrid</a>, which went on sale on the U.S. in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> VW also announced plans to introduce <a href="/wiki/Diesel_fuel" title="Diesel fuel">diesel</a>-electric hybrid versions of its most popular models in 2012, beginning with the new <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Jetta" title="Volkswagen Jetta">Jetta</a>, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Golf" title="Volkswagen Golf">Golf Hybrid</a> in 2013 together with hybrid versions of the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Polo" title="Volkswagen Polo">Passat</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parkers_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Parkers-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AECs_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-AECs-95">[95]</a></sup> Other gasoline-electric hybrids released in the U.S. in 2011 were the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lexus_CT_200h" title="Lexus CT 200h">Lexus CT 200h</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infiniti_M35_Hybrid" title="Infiniti M35 Hybrid">Infiniti M35 Hybrid</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyundai_Sonata_Hybrid" title="Hyundai Sonata Hybrid">Hyundai Sonata Hybrid</a> and its siblling the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kia_Optima_Hybrid" title="Kia Optima Hybrid">Kia Optima Hybrid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT0410_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT0410-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peugeot_3008_HYbrid4" title="Peugeot 3008 HYbrid4">Peugeot 3008 HYbrid4</a> was launched in the European market in 2012, becoming the world's first <a href="/wiki/Mass_production" title="Mass production">production</a> <a href="/wiki/Diesel_engine" title="Diesel engine">diesel</a>-electric hybrid. According to <a href="/wiki/Peugeot" title="Peugeot">Peugeot</a> the new hybrid delivers a <a href="/wiki/Fuel_economy_in_automobiles" title="Fuel economy in automobiles">fuel economy</a> of up to 62 miles per US gallon (3.8 L/100 km; 74 mpg<sub>‑imp</sub>) and CO<sub>2</sub> emissions of 99g/km on the European test cycle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2012_Toyota_Prius_c_--_05-23-2012_2.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1326" data-file-width="1774" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/2012_Toyota_Prius_c_--_05-23-2012_2.JPG/220px-2012_Toyota_Prius_c_--_05-23-2012_2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/2012_Toyota_Prius_c_--_05-23-2012_2.JPG/330px-2012_Toyota_Prius_c_--_05-23-2012_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/2012_Toyota_Prius_c_--_05-23-2012_2.JPG/440px-2012_Toyota_Prius_c_--_05-23-2012_2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2012_Toyota_Prius_c_--_05-23-2012_2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius_c" title="Toyota Prius c">Toyota Prius c</a> was released in the U.S. in March 2012, and was launched in Japan as Toyota Aqua in December 2011.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius_v" title="Toyota Prius v">Toyota Prius v</a>, launched in the U.S. in October 2011, is the first spinoff from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prius" title="Prius">Prius</a> family. Sales in Japan began in May 2011 as the Prius Alpha. The European version, named Prius +, was launched in June 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> The Prius Aqua was launched in Japan in December 2011, and was released as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius_c" title="Toyota Prius c">Toyota Prius c</a> in the U.S. in March 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaunchUS_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-LaunchUS-101">[101]</a></sup> The Prius c was launched in Australia in April 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> The production version of the 2012 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Yaris_Hybrid" title="Toyota Yaris Hybrid">Toyota Yaris Hybrid</a> went on sale in Europe in June 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other hybrids released in the U.S. during 2012 are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audi_Q5_Hybrid" title="Audi Q5 Hybrid">Audi Q5 Hybrid</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BMW_5_Series_ActiveHybrid" title="BMW 5 Series ActiveHybrid">BMW 5 Series ActiveHybrid</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BMW_3_series_Hybrid" title="BMW 3 series Hybrid">BMW 3 series Hybrid</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ford_C-Max_Hybrid" title="Ford C-Max Hybrid">Ford C-Max Hybrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acura_ILX" title="Acura ILX">Acura ILX Hybrid</a>. Also during 2012 were released the next generation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Camry_hybrid" title="Toyota Camry hybrid">Toyota Camry Hybrid</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_Hybrid#Second_generation" title="Ford Fusion Hybrid">Ford Fusion Hybrid</a>, both of which offer significantly improved fuel economy in comparison with their previous generations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USales0912_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-USales0912-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC0812_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-GCC0812-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The 2013 models of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Avalon_Hybrid" title="Toyota Avalon Hybrid">Toyota Avalon Hybrid</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Jetta_Hybrid" title="Volkswagen Jetta Hybrid">Volkswagen Jetta Hybrid</a> were released in the U.S. in December 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2012US_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2012US-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p>Global sales of the Toyota Prius liftback passed the 3 million milestone in June 2013. The Prius liftbak is available in almost 80 countries and regions, and it is the world's best-selling hybrid electric vehicle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prius3mi_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-Prius3mi-107">[107]</a></sup> Toyota released the hybrid versions of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Corolla_Axio" title="Toyota Corolla Axio">Corolla Axio</a> sedan and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corolla_Fielder" title="Corolla Fielder">Corolla Fielder</a> station wagon in Japan in August 2013. Both cars are equipped with a 1.5-liter hybrid system similar to the one used in the Prius c.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2018_Toyota_Prius_Excel_VVT-i_CVT_1.8.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1808" data-file-width="3997" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/2018_Toyota_Prius_Excel_VVT-i_CVT_1.8.jpg/220px-2018_Toyota_Prius_Excel_VVT-i_CVT_1.8.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/2018_Toyota_Prius_Excel_VVT-i_CVT_1.8.jpg/330px-2018_Toyota_Prius_Excel_VVT-i_CVT_1.8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/2018_Toyota_Prius_Excel_VVT-i_CVT_1.8.jpg/440px-2018_Toyota_Prius_Excel_VVT-i_CVT_1.8.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2018_Toyota_Prius_Excel_VVT-i_CVT_1.8.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius#Fourth_generation_(2015–present)" title="Toyota Prius">fourth generation Prius</a> was released in Japan in December 2015.</div></div></div>
<p>Sales of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honda_Vezel_Hybrid" title="Honda Vezel Hybrid">Honda Vezel Hybrid</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SUV" title="SUV">SUV</a> began in Japan began in December 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC122013_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-GCC122013-109">[109]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Range_Rover_Hybrid" title="Range Rover Hybrid">Range Rover Hybrid</a> diesel-powered electric hybrid was unveiled at the 2013 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Motor_Show" title="Frankfurt Motor Show">Frankfurt Motor Show</a>, and retail deliveries in Europe are slated to start in early 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford Motor Company</a>, the world's second largest manufacturer of hybrids after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Motor_Corporation" title="Toyota Motor Corporation">Toyota Motor Corporation</a>, reached the milestone of 400,000 hybrid electric vehicles produced in November 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> After 18 years since the introduction of hybrid cars, Japan became in 2014 the first country to reach sales of over 1 million hybrid cars in a single year, and also the Japanese market surpassed the United States as the world's largest hybrid market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HEV2014JAp_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-HEV2014JAp-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1miHEVjap_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-1miHEVjap-113">[113]</a></sup>
</p><p>The redesigned and more efficiente <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius#Fourth_generation_(2015–present)" title="Toyota Prius">fourth generation Prius</a> was released for retail customers in Japan in December 2015. The launch in North American market is scheduled for January 2016, and February in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PriusTopHEV_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-PriusTopHEV-114">[114]</a></sup> The 2016 <a href="/wiki/Model_year" title="Model year">model year</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius_Eco" title="Toyota Prius Eco">Prius Eco</a> surpassed the 2000 <a href="/wiki/Honda_Insight#First_generation_(1999–2006)" title="Honda Insight">first generation Honda Insight</a> as the all-time <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EPA" title="EPA">EPA</a>-rated most fuel efficient gasoline-powered car available in the U.S. without <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">plug-in capability</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAMost2015_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPAMost2015-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016PriusEcoTop_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-2016PriusEcoTop-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAtop10_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPAtop10-117">[117]</a></sup> In late 2017 Chevy introduced the Chevy ZH2 that runs off of hydrogen fuel cells. The ZH2 was built especially for the U.S.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sales_and_rankings">Sales and rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Sales and rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As of  January 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, more than 12 million hybrid electric vehicles have been sold worldwide since their inception in 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US4mi_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-US4mi-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC10miHEVs_5-7"><a href="#cite_note-TMC10miHEVs-5">[5]</a></sup> As of  April 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Japan ranked as the market leader with more than 5 million hybrids sold, followed by the United States with cumulative sales of over 4 million units since 1999, Europe with about 1.5 million, and the rest of the world with combined sales of over 500,000 hybrids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US4mi_6-4"><a href="#cite_note-US4mi-6">[6]</a></sup> As of  August 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, more than 130,000 hybrids have been sold in Canada, of which, over 100,000 are Toyota and Lexus models.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> In Australia, over 50,000 Lexus and Toyota models have been sold through February 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC092014_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-TMC092014-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of  January 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, global hybrid sales led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Motor_Company" title="Toyota Motor Company">Toyota Motor Company</a> (TMC) with over 10 million <a href="/wiki/Lexus" title="Lexus">Lexus</a> and Toyota hybrids sold;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC10miHEVs_5-8"><a href="#cite_note-TMC10miHEVs-5">[5]</a></sup> followed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honda_Motor_Co.,_Ltd." title="Honda Motor Co., Ltd.">Honda Motor Co., Ltd.</a> with cumulative global sales of more than 1.35 million hybrids as of  June 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Honda1mi_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Honda1mi-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Honda2013_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Honda2013-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Honda062014_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Honda062014-12">[12]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Corporation" title="Ford Motor Corporation">Ford Motor Corporation</a> with over 424,000 hybrids sold in the United States through June 2015, of which, around 10% are <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrids</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ford200K_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ford200K-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2012US_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2012US-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2013US_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2013US-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2014US_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2014US-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales062015US_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sales062015US-17">[17]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Group" title="Hyundai Group">Hyundai Group</a> with cumulative global sales of 200,000 hybrids as of  March 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, including both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyundai_Motors" title="Hyundai Motors">Hyundai Motors</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kia_Motors" title="Kia Motors">Kia Motors</a> hybrid models;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hyundai200K_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hyundai200K-18">[18]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PSA_Peugeot_Citro%C3%ABn" title="PSA Peugeot Citroën">PSA Peugeot Citroën</a> with over 50,000 diesel-powered hybrids sold in Europe through December 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PSA50K_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-PSA50K-121">[121]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2016_Toyota_Prius_(ZVW50R)_Hybrid_liftback_(2016-04-02)_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2191" data-file-width="3795" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/2016_Toyota_Prius_%28ZVW50R%29_Hybrid_liftback_%282016-04-02%29_01.jpg/220px-2016_Toyota_Prius_%28ZVW50R%29_Hybrid_liftback_%282016-04-02%29_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/2016_Toyota_Prius_%28ZVW50R%29_Hybrid_liftback_%282016-04-02%29_01.jpg/330px-2016_Toyota_Prius_%28ZVW50R%29_Hybrid_liftback_%282016-04-02%29_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/2016_Toyota_Prius_%28ZVW50R%29_Hybrid_liftback_%282016-04-02%29_01.jpg/440px-2016_Toyota_Prius_%28ZVW50R%29_Hybrid_liftback_%282016-04-02%29_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2016_Toyota_Prius_(ZVW50R)_Hybrid_liftback_(2016-04-02)_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">Toyota Prius</a> is the all-time top-selling hybrid in both Japan and the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US4mi_6-5"><a href="#cite_note-US4mi-6">[6]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>TMC experienced record sales of hybrid cars during 2013, with 1,279,400 units sold worldwide, and it took nine months to achieve one million hybrid sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC6mi_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-TMC6mi-122">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prius062013_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Prius062013-123">[123]</a></sup> Again in 2014, TMC sold a record one million hybrids in nine months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC7mi_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-TMC7mi-124">[124]</a></sup> Toyota hybrids combined with Lexus models reached 1 million units in May 2007,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Toyota0909_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Toyota0909-125">[125]</a></sup> and the U.S. reached the 1 million mark of sales of both brands by February 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Toyota0109_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Toyota0109-126">[126]</a></sup> Worldwide sales of TMC hybrids totaled over 2 million vehicles by August 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Toyota0909_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-Toyota0909-125">[125]</a></sup> 3 million units by February 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> 5 million in March 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC5miHEVs_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-TMC5miHEVs-128">[128]</a></sup> 7 million in September 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC7mi_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-TMC7mi-124">[124]</a></sup> and the 8 million mark in July 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC8miHEVs_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-TMC8miHEVs-129">[129]</a></sup> The 9 million sales mark was reached in April 2016, again, selling one million hybrids in just ninth months,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC9miHEVs_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-TMC9miHEVs-130">[130]</a></sup> and the 10 million milestone in January 2017, achieved one more time just nine months after the previous million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC10miHEVs_5-9"><a href="#cite_note-TMC10miHEVs-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ford experienced record sales of its hybrids models in the U.S. during 2013, with almost 80,000 units sold, almost triple the 2012 total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> During the second quarter of 2013 Ford achieved its best hybrid sales quarter ever, up 517% over the same quarter of 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PR_Newswire_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Newswire-132">[132]</a></sup> In 2013 Toyota’s hybrid market share in the U.S. declined from 2012 totals due to new competition, particularly from Ford with the arrival of new products such as the C-Max Hybrid and the new styling of the Fusion. Except for the Prius c, sales of the other models of the Prius family and the Camry Hybrid suffered a decline from 2012, while the Fusion Hybrid experienced a 164.3% increase from 2012, and C-Max Hybrid sales climbed 156.6%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2013US_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2013US-15">[15]</a></sup> During 2013 Ford increased its market share of the American hybrid market from 7.5% in 2012 to 14.7% in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2013US_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2013US-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FordUSShare092013_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-FordUSShare092013-133">[133]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of  January 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, global hybrid sales are led by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prius_family" title="Prius family">Prius family</a>, with cumulative sales of 6.0361 million units (excluding plug-in hybrids) representing 60% of the 10 million hybrids sold worldwide by Toyota and Lexus since 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC10miHEVs_5-10"><a href="#cite_note-TMC10miHEVs-5">[5]</a></sup> As of  January 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">Toyota Prius</a> liftback is the leading model of the Toyota brand with cumulative sales of 3.985 million units. Ranking second is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius_c" title="Toyota Prius c">Toyota Aqua/Prius c</a>, with global sales of 1.380 million units, followed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius_v" title="Toyota Prius v">Prius v/α/+</a> with 671,200, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Camry_Hybrid" title="Toyota Camry Hybrid">Camry Hybrid</a> with 614,700 units, the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Auris" title="Toyota Auris">Toyota Auris</a> with 378,000 units, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Yaris_Hybrid" title="Toyota Yaris Hybrid">Toyota Yaris Hybrid</a> with 302,700.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC10miHEVs_5-11"><a href="#cite_note-TMC10miHEVs-5">[5]</a></sup> U.S. sales of the Toyota Prius reached the 1.0 million milestone in early April 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US1million_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-US1million-134">[134]</a></sup> and cumulative sales of the Prius in Japan exceeded the 1 million mark in August 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JP1million_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-JP1million-135">[135]</a></sup> As of  January 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, sales of the Prius liftback totaled over 1.8 million units in Japan and 1.75 million in the United States, ranking as the all-time best-selling hybrid car in both countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC10miHEVs_5-12"><a href="#cite_note-TMC10miHEVs-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US4mi_6-6"><a href="#cite_note-US4mi-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>Global sales of Lexus brand hybrid vehicles worldwide reached the 500 thousand mark in November 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lexus500K_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lexus500K-136">[136]</a></sup> The 1 million sales milestone was achieved in March 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lexus1mi_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lexus1mi-19">[19]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lexus_RX" title="Lexus RX">Lexus RX 400h/RX 450h</a> ranks as the top-selling Lexus hybrid with 363,000 units delivered worldwide as of  January 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, followed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lexus_CT_200h" title="Lexus CT 200h">Lexus CT 200h</a> with 290,800 units, and the <a href="/wiki/Lexus_ES#Sixth_generation" title="Lexus ES">Lexus ES 300h</a> with 143,200 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC10miHEVs_5-13"><a href="#cite_note-TMC10miHEVs-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japanese_market">Japanese market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Japanese market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of  April 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Japan ranks as the world's market leader with more than 5 million hybrids sold since 1997, representing around 45% of cumulative global hybrid sales since their inception.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US4mi_6-7"><a href="#cite_note-US4mi-6">[6]</a></sup> After 18 years since their introduction in the Japanese market, annual hybrid sales surpassed the 1 million mark for the first time in 2014. With cumulative sales of over 4 million hybrids through December 2014, Japan surpassed the United States as the world's largest hybrid market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US4mi_6-8"><a href="#cite_note-US4mi-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HEV2014JAp_112-2"><a href="#cite_note-HEV2014JAp-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1miHEVjap_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-1miHEVjap-113">[113]</a></sup> It was also the first time that all eight major Japanese manufacturers offered hybrid vehicles in their lineup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1miHEVjap_113-2"><a href="#cite_note-1miHEVjap-113">[113]</a></sup>
</p><p>Japan also has the world's highest hybrid <a href="/wiki/Market_penetration" title="Market penetration">market penetration</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JapanHEVcapital_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-JapanHEVcapital-7">[7]</a></sup> The hybrid <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a> of new car sales began to increase significantly in 2009, when the government implemented aggressive fiscal incentives for fuel efficient vehicles and the third generation Prius was introduced. That year, the hybrid market share of new car sales in the country, including kei cars, jumped from less than 5% in 2008 to over 10% in 2009. If only conventional passenger cars are accounted for, the hybrid market share was about 15%. By 2013 the hybrid market share accounted for more than 30% of the 2.9 million standard passenger vehicles sold, and about 20% of the 4.5 million passenger vehicles including kei cars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JapHEVshare_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-JapHEVshare-8">[8]</a></sup> Sales of standard cars in 2016 totaled 1.49 million units, with the hybrid segment achieving a record 38% market share. Accounting for kei cars, hybrids achieved a market share of 25.7% of new passenger car sales, up from 22.3% in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JapanHEVcapital_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-JapanHEVcapital-7">[7]</a></sup> In 2016 every one of the standard cars listed in the Japanese top-20 best-selling car ranking had a hybrid version on sale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JapanHEVcapital_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-JapanHEVcapital-7">[7]</a></sup> and the two top-selling standard cars were models available only as a hybrid, the Toyota Prius and the Toyota Aqua.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Japan2016Top30_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-Japan2016Top30-182">[182]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a>'s hybrid sales in Japan since 1997, including both Toyota and Lexus models, passed the 1 million mark in July 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Toyota0710_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-Toyota0710-183">[183]</a></sup> 2 million in October 2012,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMCSales1012_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-TMCSales1012-184">[184]</a></sup> and topped the 3 million mark in March 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC092014_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-TMC092014-119">[119]</a></sup> As of  January 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, TMC hybrid sales in the country totaled 4,853,000 vehicles, of which, only 4,900 units are commercial vehicles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC10miHEVs_5-14"><a href="#cite_note-TMC10miHEVs-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC10mi_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-TMC10mi-185">[185]</a></sup> Cumulative sales of the original Prius in Japan reached the 1 million mark in August 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JP1million_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-JP1million-135">[135]</a></sup> Sales of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prius_family" title="Prius family">Prius family</a> vehicles totaled 3,435,800 units through January 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC10miHEVs_5-15"><a href="#cite_note-TMC10miHEVs-5">[5]</a></sup> The Prius liftback is the top-selling model with 1,812,800 units, followed by the Aqua with 1,154,500 units, the Prius α with 446,400, and the Prius plug-in with 22,100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC10miHEVs_5-16"><a href="#cite_note-TMC10miHEVs-5">[5]</a></sup> Cumulative sales of <a href="/wiki/Honda" title="Honda">Honda</a>'s hybrid vehicles since November 1999 reached 25,239 units by January 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HondaHEV09_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-HondaHEV09-186">[186]</a></sup> and in March 2010, Honda announced that the new 2010 <a href="/wiki/Honda_Insight" title="Honda Insight">Insight</a> broke through 100,000 sales in Japan in just one year after its introduction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Insight100K_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-Insight100K-187">[187]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toyota_PRIUS_%CE%B1_G_%22Touring_Selection%22_(ZVW40)_front.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1874" data-file-width="2526" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Toyota_PRIUS_%CE%B1_G_%22Touring_Selection%22_%28ZVW40%29_front.JPG/220px-Toyota_PRIUS_%CE%B1_G_%22Touring_Selection%22_%28ZVW40%29_front.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Toyota_PRIUS_%CE%B1_G_%22Touring_Selection%22_%28ZVW40%29_front.JPG/330px-Toyota_PRIUS_%CE%B1_G_%22Touring_Selection%22_%28ZVW40%29_front.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Toyota_PRIUS_%CE%B1_G_%22Touring_Selection%22_%28ZVW40%29_front.JPG/440px-Toyota_PRIUS_%CE%B1_G_%22Touring_Selection%22_%28ZVW40%29_front.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toyota_PRIUS_%CE%B1_G_%22Touring_Selection%22_(ZVW40)_front.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius_%CE%B1" title="Toyota Prius α">Toyota Prius α</a> was launched in Japan in May 2011.</div></div></div>
<p>Hybrid sales in Japan almost tripled in 2009 as compared to 2008 as a result of government incentives that included a <a href="/wiki/Scrappage_program#Japan" title="Scrappage program">scrappage program</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle#Japan" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">tax breaks</a> on hybrid vehicles and other low-emission cars and trucks, and a higher levy on gasoline that rose prices in the order of US$4.50.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAToday_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Polk2009_181-1"><a href="#cite_note-Polk2009-181">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Japan_US_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-Japan_US-188">[188]</a></sup> New hybrid car sales jumped from 94,259 in 2008<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dashboard08_137-1"><a href="#cite_note-dashboard08-137">[137]</a></sup> to 334,000 in 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tot2009_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tot2009-141">[141]</a></sup> and hybrid sales in 2009 represented around 10% of new vehicles sales in Japan. In contrast, the U.S. market share was 2.8% for the same year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAToday_59-2"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-59">[59]</a></sup> These record sales allowed Japan to surpass the U.S. in total new hybrid sales, with the Japanese market representing almost half (48%) of the worldwide hybrid sales in 2009 while the U.S. market represented 42% of global sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tot2009_141-2"><a href="#cite_note-Tot2009-141">[141]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">Toyota Prius</a> became the first hybrid to top annual new car sales in Japan with 208,876 units sold in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAToday_59-3"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTPrius10_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTPrius10-189">[189]</a></sup> The Insight ranked fifth in overall sales in 2009 with 93,283 units sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAToday_59-4"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>A total of 315,669 Priuses were sold domestically in 2010, making the Prius the country's best-selling vehicle for the second straight year. Also the Prius broke Japan's annual sales record for a single model for the first time in 20 years, surpassing the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Corolla" title="Toyota Corolla">Toyota Corolla</a>, which in 1990 set the previous sales record with 300,008 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jap2010_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jap2010-190">[190]</a></sup> The Prius sold 252,528 units in 2011, becoming the best-selling vehicle for the third-consecutive year. This figure includes sales of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prius_%CE%B1" title="Prius α">Prius α</a>, launched in May 2011, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Aqua" title="Toyota Aqua">Toyota Aqua</a>, launched in December. Despite keeping to the top-selling spot, total Prius sales for 2011 were 20% lower than 2010 due partly to the disruptions caused by the March <a href="/wiki/2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2011 Tōhoku earthquake and tsunami">2011 Tōhoku earthquake and tsunami</a>, and also because government incentives for hybrid cars were scaled back.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jap2011_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jap2011-191">[191]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> Nevertheless, during the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_year#Japan" title="Fiscal year">Japanese fiscal year</a> (April 1, 2011 through March 31, 2012), hybrid vehicles accounted for 16% of all new car sales in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> In May 2012, hybrid sales reached a record market share of 19.7% of new car sales in the country, including <a href="/wiki/Kei_car" title="Kei car">kei cars</a>. Sales were led by the conventional Prius followed by the Toyota Aqua. Also during this month, hybrid sales represented 25% of Honda sales and 46% of Toyota sales in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toyota_Aqua_103.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1280" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Toyota_Aqua_103.JPG/220px-Toyota_Aqua_103.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Toyota_Aqua_103.JPG/330px-Toyota_Aqua_103.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Toyota_Aqua_103.JPG/440px-Toyota_Aqua_103.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toyota_Aqua_103.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Aqua" title="Toyota Aqua">Toyota Aqua</a> has been the top-selling new car in Japan for three years running, from 2013 to 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TopJap2013_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-TopJap2013-195">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TopJap2013_2014_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-TopJap2013_2014-196">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TopJap2015_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-TopJap2015-197">[197]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Aqua" title="Toyota Aqua">Toyota Aqua</a>, released in December 2011, ranked as the second top-selling new car in Japan in 2012 after the conventional Prius.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> Totaling 262,367 units sold in 2013, the Aqua topped new car sales in Japan in 2013, including kei car sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TopJap2013_195-1"><a href="#cite_note-TopJap2013-195">[195]</a></sup> And with 233,209 units sold during 2014, down 11.1% from 2013, the Aqua was the top-selling new car in Japan for the second consecutive year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TopJap2013_2014_196-1"><a href="#cite_note-TopJap2013_2014-196">[196]</a></sup> Again in 2015, with 215,525 units sold, down 7.6% from 2014, the Aqua ranked as the top-selling new car in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TopJap2015_197-1"><a href="#cite_note-TopJap2015-197">[197]</a></sup> The Toyota Aqua not only was the best-selling new car in Japan for three years running, from 2013 to 2015,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TopJap2013_195-2"><a href="#cite_note-TopJap2013-195">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TopJap2013_2014_196-2"><a href="#cite_note-TopJap2013_2014-196">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TopJap2015_197-2"><a href="#cite_note-TopJap2015-197">[197]</a></sup> but it is considered the most successful nameplate launch in the Japanese market of the last 20 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Last20yr_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-Last20yr-199">[199]</a></sup> In the first quarter of 2016, the Prius liftback surpassed the Aqua as the best-selling new car,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TopJap1Q2016_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-TopJap1Q2016-200">[200]</a></sup> the Prius ended 2016 as the best-selling standard car in the Japanese market with 248,258 units, followed by the Aqua with 168,208 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Japan2016Top30_182-1"><a href="#cite_note-Japan2016Top30-182">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Japan2016_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-Japan2016-201">[201]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="American_market">American market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: American market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicles_in_the_United_States" title="Hybrid electric vehicles in the United States">Hybrid electric vehicles in the United States</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_HEV_market_share_1999_2014.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="987" data-file-width="1316" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/US_HEV_market_share_1999_2014.png/325px-US_HEV_market_share_1999_2014.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/US_HEV_market_share_1999_2014.png/488px-US_HEV_market_share_1999_2014.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/US_HEV_market_share_1999_2014.png/650px-US_HEV_market_share_1999_2014.png 2x" width="325"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_HEV_market_share_1999_2014.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>HEV <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a> of new car sales in the U.S. between 1999 and 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2012US_14-4"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2012US-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2013US_15-4"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2013US-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2014US_16-4"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2014US-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2015US_142-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2015US-142">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2011US_143-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2011US-143">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DoEHEV_144-4"><a href="#cite_note-DoEHEV-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2017US_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2017US-202">[202]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The market of <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicles_in_the_United_States" title="Hybrid electric vehicles in the United States">hybrid electric vehicles in the United States</a> is the second largest in the world after Japan, and represents about 36% of the more than 11 million hybrid sold worldwide through April 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US4mi_6-9"><a href="#cite_note-US4mi-6">[6]</a></sup> Cumulative sales passed 2 million units in May 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US2mi_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-US2mi-203">[203]</a></sup> the 3 million mark in October 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US3miHEVs_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-US3miHEVs-204">[204]</a></sup> and 4 million in April 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US4mi_6-10"><a href="#cite_note-US4mi-6">[6]</a></sup> Sales of hybrid vehicles in the U.S. began to decline following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" title="Financial crisis of 2007–08">financial crisis of 2007–08</a>, and after a short recovery, began to decline again in 2014 due to <a href="/wiki/2010s_oil_glut" title="2010s oil glut">low gasoline prices</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US4mi_6-11"><a href="#cite_note-US4mi-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2014US_16-5"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2014US-16">[16]</a></sup> Hybrid sales in the American market achieved its highest <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a> ever in 2013, capturing 3.19% of new car sales that year. At the end of 2015 the hybrid take rate had fallen to 2.21%, dropped to 1.99% in 2016, and slightly recovered to 2.13% in 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US4mi_6-12"><a href="#cite_note-US4mi-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales042016US_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sales042016US-205">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2017US_202-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2017US-202">[202]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:U.S_top_selling_HEVs_by_market_share.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="692" data-file-width="774" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/U.S_top_selling_HEVs_by_market_share.png/275px-U.S_top_selling_HEVs_by_market_share.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/U.S_top_selling_HEVs_by_market_share.png/413px-U.S_top_selling_HEVs_by_market_share.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/U.S_top_selling_HEVs_by_market_share.png/550px-U.S_top_selling_HEVs_by_market_share.png 2x" width="275"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:U.S_top_selling_HEVs_by_market_share.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicles_in_the_United_States" title="Hybrid electric vehicles in the United States">U.S. best selling HEV models</a> in 2014 by <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2014US_16-6"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2014US-16">[16]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Since their inception in 1999, a total of 4,058,258 hybrid electric automobiles and <a href="/wiki/Sport_utility_vehicle" title="Sport utility vehicle">sport utility vehicles</a> have been sold in the country through May 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US4mi_6-13"><a href="#cite_note-US4mi-6">[6]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius_family" title="Toyota Prius family">Toyota Prius family</a> is the market leader with 1,932,805 units sold through April 2016, representing a 48.0% <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a> of total hybrid sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2012US_14-5"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2012US-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2013US_15-5"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2013US-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2014US_16-7"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2014US-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2015US_142-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2015US-142">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2011US_143-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2011US-143">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DoEHEV_144-5"><a href="#cite_note-DoEHEV-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales042016US_205-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sales042016US-205">[205]</a></sup> The conventional <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">Toyota Prius</a> is the top-selling hybrid model, with 1,643,000 units sold through April 2016, accounting for 40.8% of all hybrids sold in the U.S. since inception.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US4mi_6-14"><a href="#cite_note-US4mi-6">[6]</a></sup> The United States accounted for 44.7% of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Motor_Company" title="Toyota Motor Company">Toyota Motor Company</a> global hybrid sales through April 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC9miHEVs_130-2"><a href="#cite_note-TMC9miHEVs-130">[130]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of  April 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, sales of the conventional Prius are followed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Camry_Hybrid" title="Toyota Camry Hybrid">Toyota Camry Hybrid</a>, with 345,640 units sold since 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Honda_Civic_Hybrid" title="Honda Civic Hybrid">Honda Civic Hybrid</a>, with cumulative sales of 234,610 vehicles since 2002, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_Hybrid" title="Ford Fusion Hybrid">Ford Fusion Hybrid</a> with 166,341 units since 2009, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius_c" title="Toyota Prius c">Toyota Prius c</a> with 165,075 units since 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US4mi_6-15"><a href="#cite_note-US4mi-6">[6]</a></sup> Among the hybrids built by American manufacturers, the siblings <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_MKZ" title="Lincoln MKZ">Lincoln MKZ</a>/<a href="/wiki/Mercury_Milan" title="Mercury Milan">Mercury Milan</a>/<a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_Hybrid" title="Ford Fusion Hybrid">Fusion Hybrids</a> rank first, with combined sales of 200,899 units since 2009 through 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2012US_14-6"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2012US-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2013US_15-6"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2013US-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2014US_16-8"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2014US-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2015US_142-3"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2015US-142">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2011US_143-3"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2011US-143">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DoEHEV_144-6"><a href="#cite_note-DoEHEV-144">[144]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> has been the state leading hybrid sales in the U.S. with 55,553 vehicles sold in 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dashboard09_179-1"><a href="#cite_note-dashboard09-179">[179]</a></sup> 74,932 in 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dashboard08_137-2"><a href="#cite_note-dashboard08-137">[137]</a></sup> and 91,417 in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dashboard07_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-dashboard07-138">[138]</a></sup> In 2009 it was followed by <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a> (15,438) and <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> (14,949).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dashboard09_179-2"><a href="#cite_note-dashboard09-179">[179]</a></sup> The top 5 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_metropolitan_area" title="United States metropolitan area">U. S. metropolitan area</a> markets for sales of hybrid electric vehicles in 2009 were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Los_Angeles_Area" title="Greater Los Angeles Area">Los Angeles</a> (26,677), <a href="/wiki/New_York_metropolitan_area" title="New York metropolitan area">New York</a> (21,193), <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">San Francisco</a> (15,799), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Metropolitan_Area" title="Washington Metropolitan Area">Washington, D.C.</a> (11,595), and <a href="/wiki/Chicago_metropolitan_area" title="Chicago metropolitan area">Chicago</a> (8,990).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dashboard09_179-3"><a href="#cite_note-dashboard09-179">[179]</a></sup> The Prius became the best selling vehicle in California in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> Again in 2013, the Prius <a href="/wiki/Nameplate" title="Nameplate">nameplate</a> was the best selling vehicle in California with 69,728 units sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Calif4Q2013_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-Calif4Q2013-208">[208]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_market">European market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: European market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2017_Toyota_Auris_Design_TSS_Hybrid_VVt-i_CVT_2.0_Front.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2432" data-file-width="4667" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/2017_Toyota_Auris_Design_TSS_Hybrid_VVt-i_CVT_2.0_Front.jpg/220px-2017_Toyota_Auris_Design_TSS_Hybrid_VVt-i_CVT_2.0_Front.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/2017_Toyota_Auris_Design_TSS_Hybrid_VVt-i_CVT_2.0_Front.jpg/330px-2017_Toyota_Auris_Design_TSS_Hybrid_VVt-i_CVT_2.0_Front.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/2017_Toyota_Auris_Design_TSS_Hybrid_VVt-i_CVT_2.0_Front.jpg/440px-2017_Toyota_Auris_Design_TSS_Hybrid_VVt-i_CVT_2.0_Front.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2017_Toyota_Auris_Design_TSS_Hybrid_VVt-i_CVT_2.0_Front.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Auris_Hybrid" title="Toyota Auris Hybrid">Toyota Auris Hybrid</a> is the top-selling hybrid electric vehicle in Europe with 427,600 units through 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC11miHEVs_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-TMC11miHEVs-209">[209]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>As of  April 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, about 1.5 million hybrids cars have been sold in Europe since their introduction, representing around 13.6% of cumulative global hybrid sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US4mi_6-16"><a href="#cite_note-US4mi-6">[6]</a></sup> Of these, Toyota and Lexus hybrids totaled around 1.1 million units (74%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC9miHEVs_130-3"><a href="#cite_note-TMC9miHEVs-130">[130]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PSA_Peugeot_Citro%C3%ABn" title="PSA Peugeot Citroën">PSA Peugeot Citroën</a> had sold over 50,000 diesel-powered hybrids in Europe through December 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PSA50K_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-PSA50K-121">[121]</a></sup> In 2014, one-fourth of all new vehicles sold by Toyota in the European Union were hybrid-electric.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUpocketbook2014_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-EUpocketbook2014-9">[9]</a></sup> The top-selling hybrid markets in 2015 were France, followed by the UK, Italy, Germany, Spain, the Netherlands, and Norway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EU4Q2015_145-6"><a href="#cite_note-EU4Q2015-145">[145]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of  December 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, hybrid vehicles accounted for 1.4% of new passenger car registrations in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU_Member_States" title="EU Member States">EU Member States</a>, up from 1.1% in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUpocketbook2014_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-EUpocketbook2014-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUpocketbook2013_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-EUpocketbook2013-210">[210]</a></sup> The Netherlands is the leading country within the Union states with a <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a> of 3.7% of total passenger car sales in 2014, though fewer hybrid vehicles were sold in the Dutch market in 2014 than in previous years. Accounting for all countries in the continent, Norway is the segment leader, with a market share of 6.9% in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUpocketbook2014_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-EUpocketbook2014-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sales of hybrids in Europe went up from around 9,000 units in 2004 to 39,880 in 2006, with Toyota accounting for 91% of hybrid sales and Honda with 3,410 units sold that year. Cumulative sales of Toyota hybrids since 2000 reached 69,674 units in 2006, while Honda hybrid sales reached over 8,000 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> By January 2009, Honda had sold 35,149 hybrids in Europe, of which 34,757 were <a href="/wiki/Honda_Civic_Hybrid" title="Honda Civic Hybrid">Honda Civic Hybrids</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HondaHEV09_186-1"><a href="#cite_note-HondaHEV09-186">[186]</a></sup> During 2008 combined sales of Toyota and Lexus hybrids in Europe were 57,819 units, representing 5.2% of total Toyota sales in the region. Toyota sales were led by Prius with 41,495 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Cumulative sales of the Toyota Prius reached 100,000 units in 2008 and the 200,000 mark was reached in July 2010. The UK has been one of the leading European markets for the Prius since its inception, with 20% of Prius sales in Europe by 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toyota_Yaris_Hybrid_Life_(XP130)_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht,_18._Juni_2012,_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1820" data-file-width="3272" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Toyota_Yaris_Hybrid_Life_%28XP130%29_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_18._Juni_2012%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/220px-Toyota_Yaris_Hybrid_Life_%28XP130%29_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_18._Juni_2012%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Toyota_Yaris_Hybrid_Life_%28XP130%29_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_18._Juni_2012%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/330px-Toyota_Yaris_Hybrid_Life_%28XP130%29_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_18._Juni_2012%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Toyota_Yaris_Hybrid_Life_%28XP130%29_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_18._Juni_2012%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/440px-Toyota_Yaris_Hybrid_Life_%28XP130%29_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_18._Juni_2012%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toyota_Yaris_Hybrid_Life_(XP130)_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht,_18._Juni_2012,_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Yaris_Hybrid" title="Toyota Yaris Hybrid">Toyota Yaris Hybrid</a>, released in 2012, is available in Europe in lieu of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prius_c" title="Prius c">Prius c</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Toyota's European hybrid sales reached 70,529 vehicles in 2010, including sales of 15,237 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Auris_Hybrid" title="Toyota Auris Hybrid">Toyota Auris Hybrids</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> Sales reached 84,839 units in 2011, including 59,161 Toyota and 25,678 Lexus hybrid vehicles. The Auris hybrid sold 32,725 units in 2011. Lexus hybrids made up 85% of total sales in Western Europe in 2011. Toyota and Lexus hybrids represented 10% percent of Toyota's European new car sales in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Toyota35mi_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-Toyota35mi-215">[215]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> TMC share of hybrid sales out of the company's total European sales climbed from 13% in 2012 to 20% during the first 11 months of 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the first nine months of 2013, over 118,000 hybrids were sold in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a> representing a 1.4% market share of new car sales in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup>  A total of 192,664 hybrid cars were sold in the European Union and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EFTA" title="EFTA">EFTA</a> countries in 2014. Sales increased 21.5% in 2015, with 234,170 units sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EU4Q2015_145-7"><a href="#cite_note-EU4Q2015-145">[145]</a></sup> In 2015, gasoline-powered hybrids represented 91.6% of total hybrid registrations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europe2015_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europe2015-219">[219]</a></sup> The top-selling model in 2015 was the Toyota Auris Hybrid, with 75,810 units, up 13.0% from 2014; followed by the Yaris Hybrid with 68,902 units, up 22% from 2014. Seven of the top ten hybrids models sold in 2015 were from either Toyota or the Lexus brand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europe2015_219-1"><a href="#cite_note-Europe2015-219">[219]</a></sup> Toyota achieved record hybrid sales in 2015 with 201,500 units delivered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC9miHEVs_130-4"><a href="#cite_note-TMC9miHEVs-130">[130]</a></sup> Hybrid registrations in the European Union and EFTA countries totaled 74,796 units during the first quarter of 2016, up 29.7% from the same quarter the previous year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EU1Q2016_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-EU1Q2016-220">[220]</a></sup>
</p><p>Cumulative TMC sales since the Prius introduction in Europe in 2000 passed the one million unit milestone in November 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EU1mi_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-EU1mi-221">[221]</a></sup>  As of  December 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the top-selling Toyota hybrids were the Auris Hybrid (427,600), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Yaris_Hybrid" title="Toyota Yaris Hybrid">Yaris Hybrid</a> (388,900), and the conventional Prius (299,100).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC11miHEVs_209-1"><a href="#cite_note-TMC11miHEVs-209">[209]</a></sup> The top-selling Lexus models are the <a href="/wiki/Lexus_RX" title="Lexus RX">Lexus RX 400h/RX 450h</a> with 111,100 units, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lexus_CT_200h" title="Lexus CT 200h">Lexus CT 200h</a> with 78,100 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC11miHEVs_209-2"><a href="#cite_note-TMC11miHEVs-209">[209]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>UK</dt></dl>
<p>Since 2006 hybrid car registrations in the UK totaled 257,404 units up to April 2016, including 11,679 diesel-electric hybrids, which were introduced in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK2015_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-UK2015-152">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK2013_14_153-2"><a href="#cite_note-UK2013_14-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK2012_13_154-1"><a href="#cite_note-UK2012_13-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK2011_12_155-1"><a href="#cite_note-UK2011_12-155">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK2010_11_156-1"><a href="#cite_note-UK2010_11-156">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK200906_157-3"><a href="#cite_note-UK200906-157">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK042016_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-UK042016-222">[222]</a></sup> The market share of the British hybrid segment climbed from 1.1% in 2010, to 1.2% in 2012, and achieved 1.5% of new car registrations in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUpocketbook2014_9-4"><a href="#cite_note-EUpocketbook2014-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2000, when the Prius was launched in the UK, 100,000 Toyota hybrids had been sold by May 2014, and almost 50,000 Lexus models since the introduction of the RX 400h in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> Honda had sold in the UK more than 22,000 hybrid cars through December 2011 since the Insight was launched in the country in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> After 15 years since the launch of the Prius in the British market, combined sales of Toyota and Lexus hybrids reached the 200,000 unit milestone in November 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup>
</p><p>A total of 37,215 hybrids were registered in 2014, and while petrol-electric hybrids increased 32.6% from 2013, diesel-electric hybrids declined 12.6%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK2013_14_153-3"><a href="#cite_note-UK2013_14-153">[153]</a></sup>  Hybrid registrations totaled a record of 44,580 units in 2015, consisting of 40,707 petrol-powered hybrids and 3,873 powered by diesel; the latter experienced a 36.3% increase from 2014, while petrol-powered hybrid grew by 18.1%. The hybrid segment market shared reached 1.69% of new car registrations in the UK that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK2015_152-2"><a href="#cite_note-UK2015-152">[152]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>France</dt></dl>
<p>A total of 165,915 hybrid cars have been registered in France between 2007 and 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2013_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2013-146">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2012_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2012-147">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2011_148-1"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2011-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2010_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2010-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA200908_150-2"><a href="#cite_note-FRA200908-150">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2007_151-1"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2007-151">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2014_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2014-226">[226]</a></sup> including 33,547 diesel-powered hybrids. French registrations account <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrid</a> together with conventional hybrids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2013_146-2"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2013-146">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2011_148-2"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2011-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2014_226-1"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2014-226">[226]</a></sup> Among <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU_Member_States" title="EU Member States">EU Member States</a>, France had the second largest hybrid market share in 2014, with 2.3% of new car sales, down from 2.6% in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUpocketbook2014_9-5"><a href="#cite_note-EUpocketbook2014-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>Diesel hybrid technology, introduced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PSA_Peugeot_Citro%C3%ABn" title="PSA Peugeot Citroën">PSA Peugeot Citroën</a> with the HYbrid4 system in 2011, represented 20.2% of the hybrid car stock sold in France between 2011 and 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2013_146-3"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2013-146">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2012_147-2"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2012-147">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2011_148-3"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2011-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2014_226-2"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2014-226">[226]</a></sup> Among the 13,340 units registered in 2011, the top-selling models in the French market were the Toyota Auris (4,740 units), the Prius (2,429 units), and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honda_Jazz_Hybrid" title="Honda Jazz Hybrid">Honda Jazz Hybrid</a> (1,857 units). The diesel-powered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peugeot_3008_HYbrid4" title="Peugeot 3008 HYbrid4">Peugeot 3008 HYbrid4</a>, launched in late 2011, sold 401 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2011_148-4"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2011-148">[148]</a></sup> Toyota led hybrid sales in the French market in 2013 with  27,536 registrations of its Yaris, Auris and Prius models, followed by the PSA group with 13,400 registrations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2013_146-4"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2013-146">[146]</a></sup> During 2014, a total of 42,813 hybrid cars and vans were registered, down 8.5% from 2013. Of these, 9,518 were diesel-electric hybrids, down 31.9% from 13,986 units a year earlier, while registrations of gasoline-electric hybrids were up 1.5%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2014_226-3"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2014-226">[226]</a></sup> The top-selling models in 2014 were the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Yaris_Hybrid" title="Toyota Yaris Hybrid">Toyota Yaris Hybrid</a> with 12,819 units, <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Auris" title="Toyota Auris">Toyota Auris</a> with 10,595 and the Peugeot 3008 with 4,189 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2014_226-4"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2014-226">[226]</a></sup> Hybrid registrations in 2014 included 1,519 <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrids</a>, with sales led by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_Outlander_P-HEV" title="Mitsubishi Outlander P-HEV">Mitsubishi Outlander P-HEV</a>, with 820 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRA2014_226-5"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2014-226">[226]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRAsales2014_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-FRAsales2014-227">[227]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>The Netherlands</dt></dl>
<p>As of  31 December 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, hybrid car registrations totaled 131,011 units, up 11.7% from 117,259 a year earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nether2015_170-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nether2015-170">[170]</a></sup> By the end of 2009 there were about 39,300 hybrid cars registered in the Netherlands, up from 23,000 the previous year. Most of the registered hybrid cars belonged to corporate fleets due to tax incentives established in the country in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NED2009_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-NED2009-228">[228]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> During the first eight months of 2013, around 65% of TMC cars sold in the Netherlands have been hybrids, with the technology particularly popular among fleet owners and taxi drivers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMCEU2013_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-TMCEU2013-230">[230]</a></sup> Following the same market trend as in 2014, more <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrids</a> were registered in 2015 (41,226) in the country than conventional hybrids (13,752).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nether2015_170-2"><a href="#cite_note-Nether2015-170">[170]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nether2014_171-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nether2014-171">[171]</a></sup>
</p><p>As a result of the tax incentives, the country has had for several years the highest hybrid <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a> among <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU_Member_States" title="EU Member States">EU Member States</a>. Hybrid sales climbed from 0.7% in 2006 and 2007 to 2.4% in 2008, and reached 4.2% in 2009. Due to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" title="Financial crisis of 2007–08">financial crisis of 2007–08</a>, the market fell for two years to 2.7% in 2011, but recovered to 4.5% in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUpocketbook2013_210-1"><a href="#cite_note-EUpocketbook2013-210">[210]</a></sup> As fewer hybrid vehicles were sold in the Dutch market in 2014 than in previous years, the hybrid segment market share fell to  3.7% of total passenger car sales in 2014. The sales decline is due to a change in the national vehicle taxation scheme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUpocketbook2014_9-6"><a href="#cite_note-EUpocketbook2014-9">[9]</a></sup> As of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Japan (~20%) and Norway (6.9%) are the only countries with a higher market share than the Netherlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JapHEVshare_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-JapHEVshare-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUpocketbook2014_9-7"><a href="#cite_note-EUpocketbook2014-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Germany</dt></dl>
<p>As of  January 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there where were  130,365 hybrid cars registered in Germany,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Germany2015_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-Germany2015-231">[231]</a></sup> up from 85,575 on the roads in January 1, 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Germany2013_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-Germany2013-232">[232]</a></sup> and 47,642 vehicles on January 1, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> Hybrid car registrations totaled a record of 24,963 units in 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GER2013_163-1"><a href="#cite_note-GER2013-163">[163]</a></sup> and declined to 22,908 in 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GER2014_162-1"><a href="#cite_note-GER2014-162">[162]</a></sup> and to 22,529 in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SalesGer2015_161-1"><a href="#cite_note-SalesGer2015-161">[161]</a></sup> The German hybrid market share climbed from 0.3% in 2010, to 0.8% in 2013, and declined 0.7% of new car registrations in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUpocketbook2014_9-8"><a href="#cite_note-EUpocketbook2014-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Spain</dt></dl>
<p>A total of 10,350 hybrid cars were registered in Spain in 2011, up 22% from 2010 sales. The top-selling hybrids were the Toyota Prius, Toyota Auris HSD and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lexus_CT_200h" title="Lexus CT 200h">Lexus CT 200h</a>, which together represented 83,2% of new hybrid car sales in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESP2011_169-1"><a href="#cite_note-ESP2011-169">[169]</a></sup> During 2012 hybrid sales remained almost constant with 10,030 units sold, representing 1.44% of new passenger cars sales that year. The top-selling car was the Prius with 3,969 units, followed by the Auris HSD (2,234) and the Lexus CT 200h (1,244). Combined sales of Toyota and Lexus models represented 89.15% of hybrid sales in the Spanish market in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESP2012_168-1"><a href="#cite_note-ESP2012-168">[168]</a></sup> Hybrid sales in 2013 increased 1.72% from 2012, with 10,294 units registered. The Toyota Auris HSD was the top-selling hybrid with 3,644 units, followed by the Prius (2,378) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Yaris_Hybrid" title="Toyota Yaris Hybrid">Yaris Hybrid</a> (1,587 ).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESP2013_167-1"><a href="#cite_note-ESP2013-167">[167]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The varieties of hybrid electric designs can be differentiated by the structure of the <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle_drivetrain" title="Hybrid vehicle drivetrain">hybrid vehicle drivetrain</a>, the fuel type, and the mode of operation.
</p><p>In 2007, several automobile manufacturers announced that future vehicles will use aspects of hybrid electric technology to reduce fuel consumption without the use of the hybrid drivetrain. Regenerative braking can be used to recapture energy and stored to power electrical accessories, such as air conditioning. Shutting down the engine at idle can also be used to reduce fuel consumption and reduce emissions without the addition of a hybrid drivetrain. In both cases, some of the advantages of hybrid electric technology are gained while additional cost and weight may be limited to the addition of larger batteries and starter motors. There is no standard terminology for such vehicles, although they may be termed <a href="/wiki/Mild_hybrid" title="Mild hybrid">mild hybrids</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Engines_and_fuel_sources">Engines and fuel sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Engines and fuel sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fossil_fuels">Fossil fuels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Fossil fuels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
